Question: 5 horses are in a race. Mr.Jain selects two of horses at random and bets on them. The probability that he selected the winning horse is # Answer option: ['A)1/5', 'B)2/5', 'C)3/5', 'D)4/5', 'E)6/5']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
The question involves calculating the probability that Mr. Jain selects the winning horse from a group of 5 horses. The key facts needed to solve this problem are the total number of horses in the race and the fact that Mr. Jain selects two horses at random. These details are essential to determine the probability of selecting the winning horse.

### Key Facts:
5 horses are in a race
Mr.Jain selects two of horses at random

### Reformatted Question:
5 horses are in a race. Mr.Jain selects two of horses at random and bets on them. The probability that he selected the winning horse is # Answer option: ['A)1/5', 'B)2/5', 'C)3/5', 'D)4/5', 'E)6/5']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
5 horses are in a race. Mr.Jain selects two of horses at random and bets on them. The probability that he selected the winning horse is # Answer option: ['A)1/5', 'B)2/5', 'C)3/5', 'D)4/5', 'E)6/5']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To determine the probability that Mr. Jain selected the winning horse, we need to consider the following facts:

1. 5 horses are in a race.
2. Mr. Jain selects two of the horses at random.

The probability that Mr. Jain selects the winning horse is the number of favorable outcomes (selecting the winning horse) divided by the total number of possible outcomes (selecting any two horses).

- Total number of horses = 5.
- Total number of ways to select 2 horses out of 5 = C(5, 2) = 10.

Now, consider the favorable outcomes:

- There is 1 winning horse.
- Mr. Jain can select the winning horse and any one of the remaining 4 horses.

The number of favorable outcomes = 4 (since he can pair the winning horse with any of the other 4 horses).

Therefore, the probability that Mr. Jain selected the winning horse is:

Probability = Number of favorable outcomes / Total number of possible outcomes = 4/10 = 2/5.

Thus, the probability that Mr. Jain selected the winning horse is {B)2/5}.
Final Answer: b)2/5
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: Silu and Meenu were walking on the road. Silu said, "I weigh 51 Kgs. How much do you weigh?" Meenu replied that she wouldn't reveal her weight directly as she is overweight. But she said, "I weigh 29 Kgs plus half of my weight. "How much does Meenu weigh? # Answer option: ['A)12', 'B)28', 'C)27', 'D)58', 'E)91']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
To determine Meenu's weight, we need to focus on the information she provides about her weight. Silu's weight is not directly relevant to solving the problem, as the question specifically asks about Meenu's weight. The key fact is Meenu's statement about her weight, which provides the necessary information to calculate it.

### Key Facts:
I weigh 29 Kgs plus half of my weight

### Reformatted Question:
Silu and Meenu were walking on the road. Silu said, "I weigh 51 Kgs. How much do you weigh?" Meenu replied that she wouldn't reveal her weight directly as she is overweight. But she said, "I weigh 29 Kgs plus half of my weight." How much does Meenu weigh? # Answer option: ['A)12', 'B)28', 'C)27', 'D)58', 'E)91']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
Silu and Meenu were walking on the road. Silu said, "I weigh 51 Kgs. How much do you weigh?" Meenu replied that she wouldn't reveal her weight directly as she is overweight. But she said, "I weigh 29 Kgs plus half of my weight." How much does Meenu weigh? # Answer option: ['A)12', 'B)28', 'C)27', 'D)58', 'E)91']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To determine Meenu's weight, we need to solve the equation based on the information provided:

Meenu said, "I weigh 29 Kgs plus half of my weight."

Let's denote Meenu's weight as \( x \).

According to the statement, Meenu's weight is 29 Kgs plus half of her weight, which can be expressed as:

\[ x = 29 + \frac{x}{2} \]

To solve for \( x \), we first eliminate the fraction by multiplying the entire equation by 2:

\[ 2x = 58 + x \]

Next, we subtract \( x \) from both sides to isolate \( x \):

\[ 2x - x = 58 \]

\[ x = 58 \]

Therefore, Meenu weighs 58 Kgs. The correct answer is {D}.
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: Three bells ring at intervals of 36 seconds, 40 seconds and 48 seconds, respectively. They start ringing together at a particular time. When they will ring together again? # Answer option: ['A)After 6 minutes', 'B)After 12 minutes', 'C)After 18 minutes', 'D)After 24 minutes', 'E)none']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
To determine when the three bells will ring together again, we need to find the least common multiple (LCM) of their ringing intervals. The key facts required to solve this problem are the intervals at which each bell rings.

### Key Facts:
36 seconds
40 seconds
48 seconds

### Reformatted Question:
Three bells ring at intervals of 36 seconds, 40 seconds and 48 seconds, respectively. They start ringing together at a particular time. When they will ring together again? # Answer option: ['A)After 6 minutes', 'B)After 12 minutes', 'C)After 18 minutes', 'D)After 24 minutes', 'E)none']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
Three bells ring at intervals of 36 seconds, 40 seconds and 48 seconds, respectively. They start ringing together at a particular time. When they will ring together again? # Answer option: ['A)After 6 minutes', 'B)After 12 minutes', 'C)After 18 minutes', 'D)After 24 minutes', 'E)none']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To determine when the three bells will ring together again, we need to find the least common multiple (LCM) of their ringing intervals: 36 seconds, 40 seconds, and 48 seconds.

Step 1: Prime Factorization
- 36 = 2^2 * 3^2
- 40 = 2^3 * 5
- 48 = 2^4 * 3

Step 2: Determine the LCM
The LCM is found by taking the highest power of each prime number that appears in the factorizations:
- The highest power of 2 is 2^4.
- The highest power of 3 is 3^2.
- The highest power of 5 is 5^1.

Thus, the LCM = 2^4 * 3^2 * 5 = 16 * 9 * 5.

Step 3: Calculate the LCM
- 16 * 9 = 144
- 144 * 5 = 720

The LCM is 720 seconds.

Step 4: Convert Seconds to Minutes
720 seconds is equivalent to 720 / 60 = 12 minutes.

Therefore, the three bells will ring together again after 12 minutes. The correct answer is {B}.
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: A box contains a certain number of balls, marked successively from 1 to n. If there are 45 different ways that two balls can be selected from the box such that the ball with number 3 marked on it is not selected, then what is the value of n? # Answer option: ['A)11', 'B)10', 'C)9', 'D)8', 'E)7']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
To determine the value of n, we need to focus on the information about the number of ways to select two balls without selecting the ball marked with number 3. The key fact here is the number of different ways to select two balls, which is given as 45. This information is essential to set up the equation needed to solve for n.

### Key Facts:
45 different ways that two balls can be selected from the box such that the ball with number 3 marked on it is not selected

### Reformatted Question:
A box contains a certain number of balls, marked successively from 1 to n. If there are 45 different ways that two balls can be selected from the box such that the ball with number 3 marked on it is not selected, then what is the value of n? # Answer option: ['A)11', 'B)10', 'C)9', 'D)8', 'E)7']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
A box contains a certain number of balls, marked successively from 1 to n. If there are 45 different ways that two balls can be selected from the box such that the ball with number 3 marked on it is not selected, then what is the value of n? # Answer option: ['A)11', 'B)10', 'C)9', 'D)8', 'E)7']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To solve this problem, we need to determine the total number of balls, n, in the box given that there are 45 different ways to select two balls without selecting the ball marked with number 3.

Step 1: Understand the problem
- We have n balls, numbered from 1 to n.
- We need to find the number of ways to select 2 balls from these n balls, excluding the ball numbered 3.

Step 2: Calculate the number of ways to select 2 balls from n-1 balls
- Since the ball numbered 3 is not selected, we are left with n-1 balls.
- The number of ways to choose 2 balls from n-1 balls is given by the combination formula C(n-1, 2).

Step 3: Set up the equation
- We know that C(n-1, 2) = 45.
- The combination formula is C(n-1, 2) = (n-1)(n-2)/2.

Step 4: Solve the equation
- Set up the equation: (n-1)(n-2)/2 = 45.
- Multiply both sides by 2 to clear the fraction: (n-1)(n-2) = 90.
- Expand the equation: n^2 - 3n + 2 = 90.
- Rearrange the equation: n^2 - 3n - 88 = 0.

Step 5: Solve the quadratic equation
- Use the quadratic formula: n = [-b ± sqrt(b^2 - 4ac)] / 2a, where a = 1, b = -3, and c = -88.
- Calculate the discriminant: b^2 - 4ac = (-3)^2 - 4(1)(-88) = 9 + 352 = 361.
- The square root of 361 is 19.
- Solve for n: n = [3 ± 19] / 2.

Step 6: Find the positive solution
- n = (3 + 19) / 2 = 22 / 2 = 11.
- n = (3 - 19) / 2 = -16 / 2 = -8 (not a valid solution since n must be positive).

Therefore, the value of n is 11.

The correct answer is {A)11}.
Final Answer: a)11
Ground Truth Answer: a

### Fact Extraction Reasoning:

These variables are all represented by 'x' in the initial scenario. The question then asks how much work can be completed by 'y' men working 'y' hours per day for 'y' days. The essential information involves the variables 'x' and 'y' and their roles in the work equation.

### Key Facts:
x men working x hours per day
x units of a work in x days
y men working y hours per day in y days

### Reformatted Question:
x men working x hours per day can do x units of a work in x days. How much work can be completed by y men working y hours per day in y days? # Answer option: ['A)x2/y2 units', 'B)y3/x2 units', 'C)x3/y2 units', 'D)y2/x2 units', 'E)None of these']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
x men working x hours per day can do x units of a work in x days. How much work can be completed by y men working y hours per day in y days? # Answer option: ['A)x2/y2 units', 'B)y3/x2 units', 'C)x3/y2 units', 'D)y2/x2 units', 'E)None of these']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To solve this problem, we need to determine the amount of work that can be completed by a different number of men working different hours per day over a different number of days.

1. **Understanding the initial condition:**
- x men working x hours per day can do x units of a work in x days.
- This implies that the total work done is \( x \times x \times x = x^3 \) units.

2. **Understanding the new condition:**
- We need to find out how much work can be completed by y men working y hours per day in y days.
- The total work done in this scenario is \( y \times y \times y = y^3 \) units.

3. **Comparing the two scenarios:**
- The work done by x men in the initial scenario is \( x^3 \) units.
- The work done by y men in the new scenario is \( y^3 \) units.

4. **Finding the ratio of work done:**
- We need to express the work done by y men in terms of the work done by x men.
- The ratio of work done by y men to the work done by x men is \( \frac{y^3}{x^3} \).

5. **Simplifying the expression:**
- The expression \( \frac{y^3}{x^3} \) can be rewritten as \( \left(\frac{y}{x}\right)^3 \).

6. **Matching with the answer options:**
- The expression \( \left(\frac{y}{x}\right)^3 \) does not directly match any of the given options.
- However, if we consider the context of the problem, the closest match to the expression \( \left(\frac{y}{x}\right)^3 \) is option B: \( y^3/x^2 \).

Therefore, the answer is {B}.
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b

--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To determine the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee a yearly profit of at least $626,400, we need to calculate the total revenue required and then find the selling price per component.

Step 1: Calculate the total number of components produced in a year.
- The company produces 420 units every month.
- Therefore, in a year, the company produces 420 units/month * 12 months = 5,040 units.

Step 2: Calculate the total production cost for a year.
- The production cost per component is $110.
- Therefore, the total production cost for a year is 5,040 units * $110/unit = $554,400.

Step 3: Calculate the total revenue required to achieve the desired profit.
- The desired yearly profit is $626,400.
- Therefore, the total revenue required is the total production cost plus the desired profit: $554,400 + $626,400 = $1,080,800.

Step 4: Calculate the minimum selling price per component.
- To find the minimum selling price per component, divide the total revenue required by the total number of components produced: $1,080,800 / 5,040 units = $214.29.

Since the selling price must be a whole number and the options provided are ['A)226', 'B)230', 'C)240', 'D)260', 'E)280'], the minimum selling price that is greater than or equal to $214.29 is $226.

Therefore, the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee the desired yearly profit is {A)226}.
Final Answer: a)226
Ground Truth Answer: b

### Reformatted Question:
One gram of a certain health food contains 9 percent of the minimum daily requirement of vitamin E and 8 percent of the minimum daily requirement of vitamin A. If vitamins E and A are to be obtained from no other source, how many grams of the health food must be eaten daily to provide at least the minimum daily requirement of both vitamins? # Answer option: ['A)8.5', 'B)10.5', 'C)12.5', 'D)14.5', 'E)16.5']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
One gram of a certain health food contains 9 percent of the minimum daily requirement of vitamin E and 8 percent of the minimum daily requirement of vitamin A. If vitamins E and A are to be obtained from no other source, how many grams of the health food must be eaten daily to provide at least the minimum daily requirement of both vitamins? # Answer option: ['A)8.5', 'B)10.5', 'C)12.5', 'D)14.5', 'E)16.5']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To determine how many grams of the health food must be eaten daily to provide at least the minimum daily requirement of both vitamins, we need to consider the percentage of each vitamin provided by one gram of the health food.

1. **Vitamin E Requirement:**
- One gram of the health food contains 9 percent of the minimum daily requirement of vitamin E.
- To meet 100% of the vitamin E requirement, we need to solve for the number of grams, \( x \), such that \( 9x = 100 \).
- Solving for \( x \), we get \( x = \frac{100}{9} \approx 11.11 \) grams.

2. **Vitamin A Requirement:**
- One gram of the health food contains 8 percent of the minimum daily requirement of vitamin A.
- To meet 100% of the vitamin A requirement, we need to solve for the number of grams, \( y \), such that \( 8y = 100 \).
- Solving for \( y \), we get \( y = \frac{100}{8} = 12.5 \) grams.

3. **Conclusion:**
- To satisfy both requirements, we need to consume the greater of the two amounts calculated, since both vitamins must meet their minimum daily requirements.
- Therefore, the number of grams needed is the maximum of 11.11 and 12.5, which is 12.5 grams.

Thus, the answer is {C)12.5}.
Final Answer: c)12.5
Ground Truth Answer: c

at 4 kmph for 12 hrs

### Reformatted Question:
A man walks at 5 kmph for 6 hrs and at 4 kmph for 12 hrs. His average speed is
# Answer option: ['A)4 1/3 km/h', 'B)7 2/3 km/h', 'C)9 ½ km/h', 'D)8 km/h', 'E)81 km/h']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
A man walks at 5 kmph for 6 hrs and at 4 kmph for 12 hrs. His average speed is
# Answer option: ['A)4 1/3 km/h', 'B)7 2/3 km/h', 'C)9 ½ km/h', 'D)8 km/h', 'E)81 km/h']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To find the average speed, we need to calculate the total distance traveled and the total time taken.

Step 1: Calculate the distance traveled at each speed.
- At 5 kmph for 6 hours:
- Distance = 5 kmph * 6 hrs = 30 km.
- At 4 kmph for 12 hours:
- Distance = 4 kmph * 12 hrs = 48 km.

Step 2: Calculate the total distance traveled.
- Total distance = 30 km + 48 km = 78 km.

Step 3: Calculate the total time taken.
- Total time = 6 hrs + 12 hrs = 18 hrs.

Step 4: Calculate the average speed.
- Average speed = Total distance / Total time = 78 km / 18 hrs = 4 1/3 km/h.

Therefore, the average speed is {A)4 1/3 km/h}.
Final Answer: a)4 1/3 km/h
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: If a man rows at the rate of 4 kmph in still water and his rate against the current is 2 kmph, then the man's rate along the current is: # Answer option: ['A)15 kmph', 'B)6 kmph', 'C)12 kmph', 'D)14 kmph', 'E)6 kmph']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
To determine the man's rate along the current, we need to know his rate in still water and his rate against the current. These two pieces of information are essential to calculate the rate along the current.

### Key Facts:
rows at the rate of 4 kmph in still water
rate against the current is 2 kmph

### Reformatted Question:
If a man rows at the rate of 4 kmph in still water and his rate against the current is 2 kmph, then the man's rate along the current is:
# Answer option: ['A)15 kmph', 'B)6 kmph', 'C)12 kmph', 'D)14 kmph', 'E)6 kmph']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
If a man rows at the rate of 4 kmph in still water and his rate against the current is 2 kmph, then the man's rate along the current is:
# Answer option: ['A)15 kmph', 'B)6 kmph', 'C)12 kmph', 'D)14 kmph', 'E)6 kmph']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To determine the man's rate along the current, we need to use the information provided:

1. The man's rowing rate in still water is 4 kmph.
2. His rate against the current is 2 kmph.

The rate against the current is calculated as the rate in still water minus the rate of the current. Therefore, we can express this as:

Rate against the current = Rate in still water - Rate of the current

Substituting the given values:

2 kmph = 4 kmph - Rate of the current

Solving for the rate of the current:

Rate of the current = 4 kmph - 2 kmph = 2 kmph

Now, to find the man's rate along the current, we add the rate of the current to his rate in still water:

Rate along the current = Rate in still water + Rate of the current

Substituting the values:

Rate along the current = 4 kmph + 2 kmph = 6 kmph

Therefore, the man's rate along the current is 6 kmph. The correct answer is {B}.
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: e

1. **Cost per bottle in cents**:
From 27 bottles of soda cost A cents, the cost per bottle is A/27 cents.

2. **Cost for B bottles in cents**:
If one bottle costs A/27 cents, then B bottles will cost B * (A/27) = AB/27 cents.

3. **Convert cents to dollars**:
Since there are 100 cents in a dollar, we convert the cost from cents to dollars by dividing by 100. Therefore, the cost in dollars is (AB/27) / 100 = AB/2700 dollars.

Thus, the cost of B bottles in dollars is given by the expression AB/2700. Therefore, the correct answer is {A)AB/2700}.

Question: The difference between simple interest and C.I. at the same rate for Rs.5000 for 2 years in Rs.72. The rate of interest is? # Answer option: ['A)10%', 'B)12%', 'C)6%', 'D)8%', 'E)4%']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
To determine the rate of interest, we need to focus on the principal amount, the time period, and the difference between the simple interest and compound interest. These are the essential elements required to solve the problem.

### Key Facts:
difference between simple interest and C.I. at the same rate for Rs.5000 for 2 years in Rs.72

### Reformatted Question:
The difference between simple interest and C.I. at the same rate for Rs.5000 for 2 years in Rs.72. The rate of interest is? # Answer option: ['A)10%', 'B)12%', 'C)6%', 'D)8%', 'E)4%']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
The difference between simple interest and C.I. at the same rate for Rs.5000 for 2 years in Rs.72. The rate of interest is? # Answer option: ['A)10%', 'B)12%', 'C)6%', 'D)8%', 'E)4%']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To find the rate of interest, we need to use the formula for the difference between compound interest (C.I.) and simple interest (S.I.) for two years. The formula for the difference is:

Difference = Principal × (Rate/100)^2

Given:
- Principal = Rs. 5000
- Difference = Rs. 72
- Time = 2 years

We need to find the rate of interest (R).

Using the formula:
Difference = Principal × (Rate/100)^2

Substitute the given values:
72 = 5000 × (R/100)^2

Rearrange to solve for R:
(R/100)^2 = 72 / 5000

(R/100)^2 = 0.0144

Take the square root of both sides:
R/100 = √0.0144

R/100 = 0.12

R = 0.12 × 100

R = 12

Therefore, the rate of interest is 12%.

The answer is {B)12%}.
Final Answer: b)12%
Ground Truth Answer: b

If 10 men liked green cars more than red, how many people took the survey? # Answer option: ['A)100', 'B)120', 'C)50', 'D)200', 'E)80']

--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To determine how many people took the survey, we need to use the information provided in the facts.

1. We know that 10 men liked green cars more than red. This means that these 10 men represent the 25% of men who preferred green cars, as 75% preferred red cars over green cars.

2. If 10 men represent 25% of the men surveyed, then the total number of men surveyed can be calculated as follows:
- Let the total number of men be \( x \).
- 25% of \( x \) is 10, so \( 0.25x = 10 \).
- Solving for \( x \), we get \( x = 10 / 0.25 = 40 \).

3. Now that we know there were 40 men surveyed, we can use 60% of the people who took the survey were women to find the total number of people surveyed.

4. If 60% of the survey participants were women, then 40% were men. We know that 40 men represent this 40%, so we can set up the equation:
- Let the total number of people surveyed be \( y \).
- 40% of \( y \) is 40, so \( 0.40y = 40 \).
- Solving for \( y \), we get \( y = 40 / 0.40 = 100 \).

Therefore, the total number of people who took the survey is 100. The answer is {A)100}.

- The frequency of the main line train is 10 minutes.

2. **Harbor Line Train Timing**:

- The main line train arrives at 5:00, 5:10, 5:20, etc.
- The harbor line train arrives at 5:02, 5:12, 5:22, etc.

4. **Determining the Probability**:
- From 5:00 to 5:02, the man will catch the main line train.
- From 5:02 to 5:10, the man will catch the harbor line train.
- This pattern repeats every 10 minutes.

5. **Calculating the Probability**:
- The time interval from 5:00 to 5:02 is 2 minutes.
- The time interval from 5:02 to 5:10 is 8 minutes.
- The total cycle is 10 minutes.

6. **Probability Calculation**:
- The probability of catching the main line train (first train) is the time interval for the main line train divided by the total cycle time.
- Probability = 2 minutes / 10 minutes = 0.2.

--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To determine the distance between A and B, we need to analyze the information given:

1. Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph.
2. He returned from B to A at a constant speed of 90 mph.
3. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it.

Let's break down the problem:

- Since Kevin was 70 miles away from B and traveling towards B at 70 mph, it would take him 1 hour to reach B from that point (70 miles / 70 mph = 1 hour).

- This means that 2 hours after reaching B, he would have completed his return trip to A. During these 2 hours, he traveled at 90 mph.

- Therefore, the distance from B to A (or A to B, since it's the same distance) is the distance Kevin covered in those 2 hours at 90 mph: 90 mph * 2 hours = 180 miles.

Thus, the distance between A and B is 180 miles. The correct answer is {A)180}.

The bill for that month would be : # Answer option: ['A)Rs.1560', 'B)Rs.1680', 'C)Rs.1840', 'D)Rs.1950', 'E)Rs.1690']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
To determine the bill for a month with 500 calls, we need to understand the relationship between the number of calls and the bill amount. The key facts are the number of calls and the corresponding bill amounts for the two given months. These facts will allow us to calculate the fixed and variable components of the bill.

### Key Facts:
540 calls made the bill is Rs.1800
620 calls are consumed then the bill becomes Rs.2040

### Reformatted Question:
The telephone bill of a certain establishment is partly fixed and partly varies as the number of calls consumed. When in a certain month 540 calls made the bill is Rs.1800. In another month 620 calls are consumed then the bill becomes Rs.2040. In another month 500 units are consumed due to more holidays. The bill for that month would be: # Answer option: ['A)Rs.1560', 'B)Rs.1680', 'C)Rs.1840', 'D)Rs.1950', 'E)Rs.1690']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
The telephone bill of a certain establishment is partly fixed and partly varies as the number of calls consumed. When in a certain month 540 calls made the bill is Rs.1800. In another month 620 calls are consumed then the bill becomes Rs.2040. In another month 500 units are consumed due to more holidays. The bill for that month would be: # Answer option: ['A)Rs.1560', 'B)Rs.1680', 'C)Rs.1840', 'D)Rs.1950', 'E)Rs.1690']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To solve this problem, we need to determine the fixed and variable components of the telephone bill.

Step 1: Establish the equations for the given data.
- From 540 calls made the bill is Rs.1800, we can write the equation:
\[ F + 540V = 1800 \]
where \( F \) is the fixed part of the bill and \( V \) is the variable cost per call.

- From 620 calls are consumed then the bill becomes Rs.2040, we can write the equation:
\[ F + 620V = 2040 \]

Step 2: Solve the system of equations to find \( F \) and \( V \).
- Subtract the first equation from the second:
\[ (F + 620V) - (F + 540V) = 2040 - 1800 \]
\[ 80V = 240 \]
\[ V = \frac{240}{80} = 3 \]

- Substitute \( V = 3 \) back into the first equation:
\[ F + 540 \times 3 = 1800 \]
\[ F + 1620 = 1800 \]
\[ F = 180 \]

Step 3: Calculate the bill for 500 calls.
- Using the values of \( F \) and \( V \), calculate the bill for 500 calls:
\[ F + 500V = 180 + 500 \times 3 \]
\[ = 180 + 1500 \]
\[ = 1680 \]

Therefore, the bill for the month with 500 calls would be Rs.1680. The correct answer is {B}.
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b

### Fact Extraction Reasoning:

### Key Facts:

reaches City B at 9am
train N leaves City B at 7am
reaches City A at 1030am

### Reformatted Question:
A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another? # Answer option: ['A)1 hr 23 min', 'B)1 hr 15 min', 'C)1 hr 8 min', 'D)56 min', 'E)55 min']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another? # Answer option: ['A)1 hr 23 min', 'B)1 hr 15 min', 'C)1 hr 8 min', 'D)56 min', 'E)55 min']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To determine when the two trains cross each other, we need to calculate the time it takes for them to meet after they start moving towards each other.

1. **Calculate the travel time for each train:**
- Train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9 am. Therefore, Train M takes 4 hours to travel from City A to City B.
- Train N leaves City B at 7 am and reaches City A at 10:30 am. Therefore, Train N takes 3.5 hours to travel from City B to City A.

2. **Determine the relative speeds of the trains:**
- Since both trains travel the same distance between City A and City B, we can assume the distance is the same for both.
- Let the distance be D. The speed of Train M is D/4, and the speed of Train N is D/3.5.

3. **Calculate the time when they meet:**
- Train M starts at 5 am, and Train N starts at 7 am. Therefore, Train M has already been traveling for 2 hours by the time Train N starts.
- In those 2 hours, Train M covers a distance of (D/4) * 2 = D/2.
- Now, the remaining distance to be covered by both trains together is D - D/2 = D/2.

4. **Calculate the time taken to cover the remaining distance:**
- The combined speed of both trains is (D/4) + (D/3.5).
- To find the time (T) it takes to cover the remaining D/2 distance, we use the formula: Distance = Speed * Time.
- D/2 = [(D/4) + (D/3.5)] * T
- Simplifying, we find T = (D/2) / [(D/4) + (D/3.5)].

5. **Solve for T:**
- T = (1/2) / [(1/4) + (1/3.5)]
- T = (1/2) / [(7/28) + (8/28)]
- T = (1/2) / (15/28)
- T = (1/2) * (28/15)
- T = 28/30
- T = 14/15 hours

6. **Convert T to minutes:**
- 14/15 hours = 14/15 * 60 minutes = 56 minutes.

Therefore, the two trains cross each other 56 minutes after Train N starts at 7 am, which is at 7:56 am. The answer is {D}.
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d

Q is the product of two prime numbers. # Answer option: ['A)I only', 'B)III only', 'C)II only', 'D)I and II only', 'E)I and III only']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
The question is about determining the properties of a positive integer Q that has exactly 5 factors. The key facts needed to answer this question are the conditions under which a number has exactly 5 factors. Specifically, the number must be the square of a prime number, as this is the only way to have exactly 5 factors. The other options (being the fourth power of a prime number or the product of two prime numbers) do not result in exactly 5 factors.

### Key Facts:
Q, a positive integer, has 5 factors

### Reformatted Question:
If Q, a positive integer, has 5 factors, which of the following must be true about Q? I. Q is the square of a prime number. II. Q is the fourth power of a prime number. III. Q is the product of two prime numbers. # Answer option: ['A)I only', 'B)III only', 'C)II only', 'D)I and II only', 'E)I and III only']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
If Q, a positive integer, has 5 factors, which of the following must be true about Q? I. Q is the square of a prime number. II. Q is the fourth power of a prime number. III. Q is the product of two prime numbers. # Answer option: ['A)I only', 'B)III only', 'C)II only', 'D)I and II only', 'E)I and III only']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To determine which statements about \( Q \) must be true, we need to consider the nature of the factors of a number.

1. **Understanding the number of factors:**
- If a number \( Q \) has exactly 5 factors, it must be structured in a specific way. The number of factors of a number \( n = p_1^{a_1} \times p_2^{a_2} \times \ldots \times p_k^{a_k} \) is given by \((a_1 + 1)(a_2 + 1)\ldots(a_k + 1)\).
- For \( Q \) to have exactly 5 factors, the product of these increments must equal 5.

2. **Analyzing the possibilities:**
- The number 5 is a prime number, so the only way to achieve a product of 5 is if one of the increments is 5 and the rest are 1. This implies that \( Q \) must be of the form \( p^4 \), where \( p \) is a prime number. This corresponds to statement II.

3. **Evaluating each statement:**
- **Statement I:** \( Q \) is the square of a prime number. If \( Q = p^2 \), the number of factors would be \((2 + 1) = 3\), not 5. Therefore, statement I is not necessarily true.
- **Statement II:** \( Q \) is the fourth power of a prime number. If \( Q = p^4 \), the number of factors would be \((4 + 1) = 5\), which matches the condition. Therefore, statement II is true.
- **Statement III:** \( Q \) is the product of two prime numbers. If \( Q = p_1 \times p_2 \), the number of factors would be \((1 + 1)(1 + 1) = 4\), not 5. Therefore, statement III is not necessarily true.

4. **Conclusion:**
- Only statement II must be true for \( Q \) to have exactly 5 factors.

Thus, the correct answer is {C)II only}.
Final Answer: c)ii only

Question: Train A leaves a station every 16 minutes and Train B leaves every 17 minutes. If both trains just left the station simultaneously, how long until they do so again? # Answer option: ['A)272 minutes', 'B)304 minutes', 'C)190 minutes', 'D)70 minutes', 'E)35 minutes']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:

### Key Facts:
Train A leaves a station every 16 minutes
Train B leaves every 17 minutes

### Reformatted Question:
Train A leaves a station every 16 minutes and Train B leaves every 17 minutes. If both trains just left the station simultaneously, how long until they do so again? # Answer option: ['A)272 minutes', 'B)304 minutes', 'C)190 minutes', 'D)70 minutes', 'E)35 minutes']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
Train A leaves a station every 16 minutes and Train B leaves every 17 minutes. If both trains just left the station simultaneously, how long until they do so again? # Answer option: ['A)272 minutes', 'B)304 minutes', 'C)190 minutes', 'D)70 minutes', 'E)35 minutes']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To determine when both trains will leave the station simultaneously again, we need to find the least common multiple (LCM) of their departure intervals.

1. **Identify the departure intervals:**
- Train A leaves a station every 16 minutes.
- Train B leaves every 17 minutes.

2. **Calculate the LCM of 16 and 17:**
- Since 16 and 17 are coprime (they have no common factors other than 1), the LCM is simply their product: 16 * 17.

3. **Perform the multiplication:**
- 16 * 17 = 272.

Therefore, both trains will leave the station simultaneously again in 272 minutes.

The correct answer is {A}.

2. According to , the astronaut weighs 182 pounds on Venus.

If m > 0, y > 0, and x is m percent of 4y, then, in terms of y, m is what percentage of x? # Answer option: ['A)y/400', 'B)4y', 'C)50y', 'D)2500/y', 'E)5000/y']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
If m > 0, y > 0, and x is m percent of 4y, then, in terms of y, m is what percentage of x? # Answer option: ['A)y/400', 'B)4y', 'C)50y', 'D)2500/y', 'E)5000/y']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To solve this problem, we need to express \( m \) as a percentage of \( x \) in terms of \( y \).

1. Start with the given information: \( x \) is \( m \) percent of \( 4y \). This can be expressed mathematically as:
\[
x = \frac{m}{100} \times 4y
\]

2. Rearrange the equation to solve for \( m \):
\[
m = \frac{100x}{4y}
\]

3. Simplify the expression:
\[
m = \frac{25x}{y}
\]

4. We need to find what percentage \( m \) is of \( x \). This means we need to express \( m \) as a fraction of \( x \) and then convert it to a percentage:
\[
\frac{m}{x} = \frac{25x/y}{x} = \frac{25}{y}
\]

5. Convert the fraction to a percentage by multiplying by 100:
\[
\frac{m}{x} \times 100 = \frac{25 \times 100}{y} = \frac{2500}{y}
\]

Thus, in terms of \( y \), \( m \) is \(\frac{2500}{y}\) percent of \( x \).

The correct answer is {D)2500/y}.
Final Answer: d)2500/y
Ground Truth Answer: d

--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To solve this problem, we need to analyze the expressions for \( L(x, y) \) and \( R(x, y) \) using the greatest integer function, denoted by \([x]\), which represents the greatest integer less than or equal to \( x \).

Given:
- \( L(x, y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y] \)
- \( R(x, y) = [2x] + [2y] \)

We need to determine if there are any positive real numbers \( x \) and \( y \) such that \( L(x, y) = R(x, y) \).

### Step-by-step Analysis:

1. **Understanding \( L(x, y) \):**
- \( [x] \) is the greatest integer less than or equal to \( x \).
- \( [y] \) is the greatest integer less than or equal to \( y \).
- \( [x + y] \) is the greatest integer less than or equal to \( x + y \).

2. **Understanding \( R(x, y) \):**
- \( [2x] \) is the greatest integer less than or equal to \( 2x \).
- \( [2y] \) is the greatest integer less than or equal to \( 2y \).

3. **Comparing \( L(x, y) \) and \( R(x, y) \):**
- For \( L(x, y) = R(x, y) \), we need:
\[
[x] + [y] + [x + y] = [2x] + [2y]
\]

4. **Exploring the Possibility:**
- Consider \( x = 0.5 \) and \( y = 0.5 \):
- \( [x] = [0.5] = 0 \)
- \( [y] = [0.5] = 0 \)
- \( [x + y] = [1.0] = 1 \)
- \( [2x] = [1.0] = 1 \)
- \( [2y] = [1.0] = 1 \)
- Thus, \( L(x, y) = 0 + 0 + 1 = 1 \) and \( R(x, y) = 1 + 1 = 2 \)

5. **Conclusion:**
- In this example, \( L(x, y) < R(x, y) \).
- It seems that for any positive real numbers \( x \) and \( y \), \( L(x, y) \) is always less than \( R(x, y) \).

Therefore, it is impossible to find any two positive real numbers \( x \) and \( y \) for which \( L(x, y) = R(x, y) \).

The correct answer is {A)L(x,y) = R(x,y)}.

1. **Calculate Bill's speed on a windy day:**
- On a normal day, Bill averages 15 mph.
- On a windy day, his speed is reduced by 4 mph.
- Therefore, on a windy day, Bill's speed is \(15 - 4 = 11\) mph.

- Bill travels for 21 minutes.
- To convert minutes to hours, divide by 60: \(\frac{21}{60} = 0.35\) hours.

### Reformatted Question:
At an election meeting 10 speakers are to address the meeting. The only protocol to be observed is that whenever they speak the pm should speak before the mp and the mp should speak before the mla. In how many ways can the meeting be held? # Answer option: ['A)10!/3', 'B)10!/6', 'C)10!/2', 'D)10!/4', 'E)10!/5']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To solve this problem, we need to determine the number of ways to arrange 10 speakers such that the protocol is observed: the pm should speak before the mp and the mp should speak before the mla.

Step 1: Understand the constraints
- We have 10 speakers in total.
- Among these speakers, there are three specific roles: pm, mp, and mla.
- The protocol requires that the pm speaks before the mp, and the mp speaks before the mla.

Step 2: Calculate the total number of arrangements without constraints
- Without any constraints, the 10 speakers can be arranged in 10! ways.

Step 3: Apply the constraints
- The constraint is that pm, mp, and mla must be in a specific order: pm before mp before mla.
- For any specific set of 3 people, there are 3! (6) possible ways to arrange them.
- Since we only want the arrangement where pm is before mp and mp is before mla, we divide the total arrangements by 3! to account for the order constraint.

Step 4: Calculate the number of valid arrangements
- The number of valid arrangements is 10! / 3!.

Therefore, the number of ways the meeting can be held, observing the protocol, is 10! / 6.

The correct answer is {B}.

Question: A certain liquid passes through a drain at a rate of w/25 gallons every x seconds. At that rate, how many minutes will it take y gallons to pass through the drain? # Answer option: ['A)y/(1200xy)', 'B)20xy/w', 'C)5xy/(12w)', 'D)w/(3xy)', 'E)3y/(wx)']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
To determine how many minutes it will take for y gallons to pass through the drain, we need to understand the rate at which the liquid is passing through the drain. The key information is the rate of flow, which is given as w/25 gallons every x seconds. This rate is essential to calculate the time required for y gallons to pass through the drain.

### Key Facts:
w/25 gallons every x seconds

### Reformatted Question:
A certain liquid passes through a drain at a rate of w/25 gallons every x seconds. At that rate, how many minutes will it take y gallons to pass through the drain? # Answer option: ['A)y/(1200xy)', 'B)20xy/w', 'C)5xy/(12w)', 'D)w/(3xy)', 'E)3y/(wx)']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
A certain liquid passes through a drain at a rate of w/25 gallons every x seconds. At that rate, how many minutes will it take y gallons to pass through the drain? # Answer option: ['A)y/(1200xy)', 'B)20xy/w', 'C)5xy/(12w)', 'D)w/(3xy)', 'E)3y/(wx)']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To solve this problem, we need to determine how many minutes it will take for y gallons to pass through the drain at the given rate.

1. **Understanding the rate**: The liquid passes through the drain at a rate of w/25 gallons every x seconds. This means in x seconds, w/25 gallons are drained.

2. **Finding the rate per second**: To find the rate per second, we divide the amount drained by the time in seconds:
\[
\text{Rate per second} = \frac{w/25}{x} = \frac{w}{25x} \text{ gallons per second}
\]

3. **Finding the rate per minute**: Since there are 60 seconds in a minute, the rate per minute is:
\[
\text{Rate per minute} = \frac{w}{25x} \times 60 = \frac{60w}{25x} = \frac{12w}{5x} \text{ gallons per minute}
\]

4. **Calculating the time to drain y gallons**: To find out how many minutes it takes to drain y gallons, we divide the total gallons by the rate per minute:
\[
\text{Time in minutes} = \frac{y}{\frac{12w}{5x}} = \frac{y \times 5x}{12w} = \frac{5xy}{12w}
\]

Thus, the number of minutes it will take for y gallons to pass through the drain is given by the expression \(\frac{5xy}{12w}\).

The correct answer is {C}.
Final Answer: c
Ground Truth Answer: c

### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
The question revolves around determining the smallest number of letters needed to uniquely code 10 different types of books using either a single letter or a pair of two different letters. ### Key Facts:

codes each book with either a single letter or a pair of two different letters

### Reformatted Question:
Amy is organizing her bookshelves and finds that she has 10 different types of books. She then codes each book with either a single letter or a pair of two different letters. If each type of book is uniquely represented by either a single letter or pair of letters, what is the smallest number of letters Amy will need to create the codes for all 10 types of books? (Assume the order of letters in a pair does not matter.) # Answer option: ['A)3', 'B)4', 'C)5', 'D)10', 'E)20']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
Amy is organizing her bookshelves and finds that she has 10 different types of books. She then codes each book with either a single letter or a pair of two different letters. If each type of book is uniquely represented by either a single letter or pair of letters, what is the smallest number of letters Amy will need to create the codes for all 10 types of books? (Assume the order of letters in a pair does not matter.) # Answer option: ['A)3', 'B)4', 'C)5', 'D)10', 'E)20']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To determine the smallest number of letters Amy will need, we need to consider both single-letter codes and pair-letter codes.

1. **Single-letter Codes**: If Amy uses single letters, each letter represents one type of book. Therefore, if she uses \( n \) letters, she can represent \( n \) types of books.

2. **Pair-letter Codes**: If Amy uses pairs of letters, each pair represents one type of book. The number of unique pairs that can be formed from \( n \) letters is given by the combination formula \( \binom{n}{2} = \frac{n(n-1)}{2} \).

3. **Total Codes**: The total number of unique codes (single letters + pairs) that can be formed from \( n \) letters is \( n + \binom{n}{2} \).

We need this total to be at least 10, as Amy has 10 different types of books.

Let's calculate for different values of \( n \):

- For \( n = 3 \):
- Single-letter codes: 3
- Pair-letter codes: \( \binom{3}{2} = 3 \)
- Total codes: \( 3 + 3 = 6 \)

- For \( n = 4 \):
- Single-letter codes: 4
- Pair-letter codes: \( \binom{4}{2} = 6 \)
- Total codes: \( 4 + 6 = 10 \)

- For \( n = 5 \):
- Single-letter codes: 5
- Pair-letter codes: \( \binom{5}{2} = 10 \)
- Total codes: \( 5 + 10 = 15 \)

Since \( n = 4 \) gives us exactly 10 codes, which is sufficient to represent all 10 types of books, the smallest number of letters needed is 4.

Therefore, the answer is {B}.
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: For bringing each copper coin from the bottom of a river, a coin-diver gets 20 cents, and for each brass coin she gets 25 cents. If after one dive, she got $3.40. What is the minimum number of copper coins that she brought? # Answer option: ['A)4', 'B)3', 'C)2', 'D)1', 'E)0']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
To determine the minimum number of copper coins the diver brought, we need to focus on the payment she receives for each type of coin and the total amount she earned. The key facts are the earnings per copper and brass coin and the total earnings from the dive.

### Key Facts:
20 cents
25 cents
$3.40

### Reformatted Question:
For bringing each copper coin from the bottom of a river, a coin-diver gets 20 cents, and for each brass coin she gets 25 cents. If after one dive, she got $3.40. What is the minimum number of copper coins that she brought? # Answer option: ['A)4', 'B)3', 'C)2', 'D)1', 'E)0']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
For bringing each copper coin from the bottom of a river, a coin-diver gets 20 cents, and for each brass coin she gets 25 cents. If after one dive, she got $3.40. What is the minimum number of copper coins that she brought? # Answer option: ['A)4', 'B)3', 'C)2', 'D)1', 'E)0']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To solve this problem, we need to determine the minimum number of copper coins the diver brought up, given the total earnings and the value of each type of coin.

1. **Understanding the Earnings:**
- The diver earns 20 cents for each copper coin.
- The diver earns 25 cents for each brass coin.
- The total earnings from the dive are $3.40, which is equivalent to 340 cents.

2. **Setting Up the Equation:**
- Let \( x \) be the number of copper coins and \( y \) be the number of brass coins.
- The equation for the total earnings is: \( 20x + 25y = 340 \).

3. **Finding the Minimum Number of Copper Coins:**
- We need to find the minimum value of \( x \) such that the equation holds true with non-negative integer values for both \( x \) and \( y \).

4. **Solving the Equation:**
- Rearrange the equation to express \( y \) in terms of \( x \):
\[
25y = 340 - 20x
\]
\[
y = \frac{340 - 20x}{25}
\]
- For \( y \) to be an integer, \( 340 - 20x \) must be divisible by 25.

5. **Checking Divisibility:**
- Calculate \( 340 \mod 25 \) to find the remainder:
\[
340 \div 25 = 13 \text{ remainder } 15
\]
- Therefore, \( 340 \equiv 15 \mod 25 \).
- We need \( 20x \equiv 15 \mod 25 \).

6. **Finding the Smallest \( x \):**
- Test small values of \( x \) to find the smallest one that satisfies the congruence:
- \( x = 0 \): \( 20 \times 0 = 0 \equiv 0 \mod 25 \)
- \( x = 1 \): \( 20 \times 1 = 20 \equiv 20 \mod 25 \)
- \( x = 2 \): \( 20 \times 2 = 40 \equiv 15 \mod 25 \)

- When \( x = 2 \), the equation \( 20x + 25y = 340 \) becomes:
\[
20 \times 2 + 25y = 340
\]
\[
40 + 25y = 340
\]
\[
25y = 300
\]
\[
y = 12
\]

7. **Conclusion:**
- The minimum number of copper coins the diver brought is 2, which satisfies the condition with \( y = 12 \) brass coins.

Therefore, the minimum number of copper coins is {C)2}.
Final Answer: c)2
Ground Truth Answer: c

Question: What is the largest integral value of 'k' for which the quadratic equation x2 - 5x + k = 0 will have two real and distinct roots? # Answer option: ['A)9', 'B)7', 'C)3', 'D)8', 'E)12']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
To determine the largest integral value of 'k' for which the quadratic equation will have two real and distinct roots, we need to focus on the condition for a quadratic equation to have real and distinct roots. This condition is that the discriminant of the quadratic equation must be greater than zero. The discriminant for the equation \(x^2 - 5x + k = 0\) is given by \(b^2 - 4ac\), where \(a = 1\), \(b = -5\), and \(c = k\). Therefore, the key fact is the expression for the discriminant: \(25 - 4k > 0\).

### Key Facts:
x2 - 5x + k = 0

### Reformatted Question:
What is the largest integral value of 'k' for which the quadratic equation x2 - 5x + k = 0 will have two real and distinct roots? # Answer option: ['A)9', 'B)7', 'C)3', 'D)8', 'E)12']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
What is the largest integral value of 'k' for which the quadratic equation x2 - 5x + k = 0 will have two real and distinct roots? # Answer option: ['A)9', 'B)7', 'C)3', 'D)8', 'E)12']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To determine the largest integral value of 'k' for which the quadratic equation x² - 5x + k = 0 will have two real and distinct roots, we need to use the discriminant condition for real and distinct roots. The discriminant of a quadratic equation ax² + bx + c = 0 is given by Δ = b² - 4ac.

For the quadratic equation to have two real and distinct roots, the discriminant must be greater than zero:

Δ = b² - 4ac > 0

In our equation, a = 1, b = -5, and c = k. Therefore, the discriminant is:

Δ = (-5)² - 4(1)(k) = 25 - 4k

We need this to be greater than zero for the roots to be real and distinct:

25 - 4k > 0

Solving this inequality for k:

25 > 4k

Divide both sides by 4:

25/4 > k

6.25 > k

Since we are looking for the largest integral value of k, we take the largest integer less than 6.25, which is 6.

Therefore, the largest integral value of 'k' for which the quadratic equation will have two real and distinct roots is 6.

The answer is not listed in the provided options, which suggests a possible oversight in the options or the problem setup. However, based on the calculation, the correct answer should be {6}.
Final Answer: 6
Ground Truth Answer: c
Question: The height of a room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5. It costs Rs.260 to paper the walls of the room with paper 50cm wide at Rs.2 per meter allowing an area of 15 sq.m for doors and windows. The height of the room is: # Answer option: ['A)2.6m', 'B)3.9m', 'C)4m', 'D)4.2m', 'E)4.4m']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
To determine the height of the room, we need to focus on the relationship between the height and the semi-perimeter, the cost and dimensions of the paper, and the area excluded for doors and windows. The ratio of the height to the semi-perimeter is crucial for calculating the height. The cost of papering the walls, the width and price of the paper, and the area allowed for doors and windows are essential for understanding the total area of the walls that need to be papered.

### Key Facts:
height of a room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5
costs Rs.260 to paper the walls
paper 50cm wide at Rs.2 per meter
allowing an area of 15 sq.m for doors and windows

### Reformatted Question:
The height of a room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5. It costs Rs.260 to paper the walls of the room with paper 50cm wide at Rs.2 per meter allowing an area of 15 sq.m for doors and windows. The height of the room is:
# Answer option: ['A)2.6m', 'B)3.9m', 'C)4m', 'D)4.2m', 'E)4.4m']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
The height of a room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5. It costs Rs.260 to paper the walls of the room with paper 50cm wide at Rs.2 per meter allowing an area of 15 sq.m for doors and windows. The height of the room is:
# Answer option: ['A)2.6m', 'B)3.9m', 'C)4m', 'D)4.2m', 'E)4.4m']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To find the height of the room, we need to use the given facts and perform some calculations.

1. **Understanding the Cost and Area:**
- The cost to paper the walls is Rs.260.
- The paper is 50cm wide at Rs.2 per meter. This means the cost per square meter of paper is Rs.4 (since 50 cm is 0.5 meters, and Rs.2 per meter means Rs.4 per square meter).

2. **Calculating the Total Area to be Papered:**
- The cost of Rs.260 at Rs.4 per square meter means the total area to be papered is 260 / 4 = 65 square meters.

3. **Adjusting for Doors and Windows:**
- We need to account for the area of doors and windows, which is 15 sq.m.
- Therefore, the total wall area is 65 + 15 = 80 square meters.

4. **Using the Ratio of Height to Semi-Perimeter:**
- The ratio of the height of the room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5.
- Let the height of the room be \( h \) and the semi-perimeter be \( s \).
- According to the ratio, \( h/s = 2/5 \), which implies \( h = (2/5) \times s \).

5. **Relating the Wall Area to Height and Perimeter:**
- The total wall area (excluding doors and windows) is 80 square meters.
- The wall area is given by the perimeter of the room times the height, i.e., \( 2 \times s \times h = 80 \).

6. **Substituting the Height in Terms of Semi-Perimeter:**
- Substitute \( h = (2/5) \times s \) into the wall area equation:
- \( 2 \times s \times (2/5) \times s = 80 \).
- Simplifying, \( (4/5) \times s^2 = 80 \).
- Solving for \( s^2 \), we get \( s^2 = 80 \times (5/4) = 100 \).
- Therefore, \( s = 10 \).

7. **Finding the Height:**
- Since \( h = (2/5) \times s \), substitute \( s = 10 \):
- \( h = (2/5) \times 10 = 4 \).

Thus, the height of the room is 4 meters. Therefore, the correct answer is {C}.
Final Answer: c

--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To solve this problem, we need to find the number based on the difference between two calculations: one using 7/8 of the number and the other using 7/18 of the number.

Let's denote the number as \( x \).

1. The correct calculation should have been 7/8 of the number, which is \(\frac{7}{8}x\).

2. The student mistakenly calculated 7/18 of the number, which is \(\frac{7}{18}x\).

3. The difference between the correct calculation and the student's calculation is given as 770.

So, we set up the equation based on the difference:

\[
\frac{7}{8}x - \frac{7}{18}x = 770
\]

To solve for \( x \), we first find a common denominator for the fractions, which is 72:

\[
\frac{63}{72}x - \frac{28}{72}x = 770
\]

Simplifying the left side:

\[
\frac{63x - 28x}{72} = 770
\]

\[
\frac{35x}{72} = 770
\]

\[
35x = 770 \times 72
\]

Calculate \( 770 \times 72 \):

\[
770 \times 72 = 55440
\]

Now, divide by 35 to solve for \( x \):

\[
x = \frac{55440}{35}
\]

Calculate \( \frac{55440}{35} \):

\[
x = 1584
\]

Thus, the number is 1584. Therefore, the answer is {A)1584}.

Which of the following is closest to the percent population increase in Boomtown over the last year? # Answer option: ['A)20%', 'B)40%', 'C)50%', 'D)65%', 'E)75%']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
To determine the percent population increase in Boomtown over the last year, we need to understand the relationship between the population growth projections and the past population. The key facts are the expected annual increase of 10% over the next two years and the condition that the population two years from now would be double the population of one year ago. These facts are essential to calculate the past year's population increase.

### Key Facts:
population to increase by 10% per year over the next two years
population two years from now would be exactly double the population of one year ago

### Reformatted Question:
Boomtown urban planners expect the city’s population to increase by 10% per year over the next two years. If that projection were to come true, the population two years from now would be exactly double the population of one year ago. --------------- End of Conversation ---------------
Boomtown urban planners expect the city’s population to increase by 10% per year over the next two years. If that projection were to come true, the population two years from now would be exactly double the population of one year ago. Which of the following is closest to the percent population increase in Boomtown over the last year? # Answer option: ['A)20%', 'B)40%', 'C)50%', 'D)65%', 'E)75%']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To solve this problem, we need to determine the percent population increase in Boomtown over the last year, given the projections for the next two years.

Step 1: Understand the projections.
According to the population is expected to increase by 10% per year over the next two years. This means if the current population is P, then:
- After one year, the population will be P * 1.10.
- After two years, the population will be P * 1.10 * 1.10 = P * 1.21.

Step 2: Relate the projections to the given condition.
We are told that the population two years from now would be exactly double the population of one year ago. Let's denote the population one year ago as X. Therefore, the population two years from now is 2X.

Step 3: Set up the equation.
From the above, we have:
P * 1.21 = 2X

Step 4: Solve for the relationship between P and X.
Rearranging the equation gives:
P = 2X / 1.21

Step 5: Determine the percent increase from X to P.
The population increased from X to P over the last year. The percent increase is given by:
((P - X) / X) * 100%

Substitute P = 2X / 1.21 into the equation:
((2X / 1.21 - X) / X) * 100% = ((2 / 1.21 - 1) * 100)%

Calculate the expression:
(2 / 1.21 - 1) * 100% ≈ (1.6529 - 1) * 100% ≈ 0.6529 * 100% ≈ 65.29%

Step 6: Choose the closest answer.
The closest percentage to 65.29% from the given options is 65%.

Therefore, the percent population increase in Boomtown over the last year is closest to {D)65%}.
Final Answer: d)65%
Ground Truth Answer: d

Question: An express electric train takes exact three seconds to enter tunnel which is 1 mile long. If train is traveling at 120 mile an hour, how long will it take to pass completely through the tunnel ? # Answer option: ['A)43 seconds', 'B)39 seconds', 'C)20 seconds', 'D)33 seconds', 'E)55 seconds']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
To determine how long it will take for the train to pass completely through the tunnel, we need to know the speed of the train and the length of the tunnel. The time it takes for the train to enter the tunnel is not directly relevant to the calculation of the total time to pass through the tunnel, but it does provide context for the speed and length relationship.

### Key Facts:
train is traveling at 120 mile an hour
tunnel which is 1 mile long

### Reformatted Question:
An express electric train takes exact three seconds to enter tunnel which is 1 mile long. If train is traveling at 120 mile an hour, how long will it take to pass completely through the tunnel? # Answer option: ['A)43 seconds', 'B)39 seconds', 'C)20 seconds', 'D)33 seconds', 'E)55 seconds']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
An express electric train takes exact three seconds to enter tunnel which is 1 mile long. If train is traveling at 120 mile an hour, how long will it take to pass completely through the tunnel? # Answer option: ['A)43 seconds', 'B)39 seconds', 'C)20 seconds', 'D)33 seconds', 'E)55 seconds']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To determine how long it will take for the train to pass completely through the tunnel, we need to consider both the length of the train and the length of the tunnel.

1. **Train Speed and Tunnel Length**:
- The train is traveling at a speed of 120 miles per hour.
- The tunnel is 1 mile long.

2. **Time to Enter the Tunnel**:
- The train takes exactly three seconds to enter the tunnel. This means the length of the train is the distance it covers in three seconds at 120 miles per hour.

3. **Calculating the Length of the Train**:
- Convert the speed from miles per hour to miles per second:
\[
\text{Speed in miles per second} = \frac{120 \text{ miles per hour}}{3600 \text{ seconds per hour}} = \frac{1}{30} \text{ miles per second}
\]
- In three seconds, the train covers:
\[
\text{Distance covered in 3 seconds} = 3 \times \frac{1}{30} = \frac{1}{10} \text{ miles}
\]
- Therefore, the length of the train is \(\frac{1}{10}\) miles.

4. **Total Distance to Pass Through the Tunnel**:
- To completely pass through the tunnel, the train must cover the length of the tunnel plus its own length:
\[
\text{Total distance} = 1 \text{ mile (tunnel)} + \frac{1}{10} \text{ mile (train)} = 1.1 \text{ miles}
\]

5. **Time to Pass Through the Tunnel**:
- Calculate the time to cover 1.1 miles at \(\frac{1}{30}\) miles per second:
\[
\text{Time} = \frac{1.1 \text{ miles}}{\frac{1}{30} \text{ miles per second}} = 1.1 \times 30 = 33 \text{ seconds}
\]

Therefore, the train will take 33 seconds to pass completely through the tunnel. The correct answer is {D}.
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d

### Key Facts:

An exam is given in a certain class. The average (arithmetic mean) of the highest score and the lowest score is equal to x. An exam is given in a certain class. The average (arithmetic mean) of the highest score and the lowest score is equal to x. If the average score for the entire class is equal to y and there are z students in the class, where z > 5, then in terms of x, y, and z, what is the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers? # Answer option: ['A)(zy – 2x)/z', 'B)(zy – 2)/z', 'C)(zx – y)/(z – 2)', 'D)(zy – 2x)/(z -2)', 'E)(zy – x)/(z + 2)']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To solve this problem, we need to find the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers, given the information about the averages and the number of students.

1. **Understanding the given averages:**
- The average of the highest score and the lowest score is equal to x. This means that if the highest score is H and the lowest score is L, then (H + L)/2 = x. Therefore, H + L = 2x.
- The average score for the entire class is equal to y. This means that the total score for all students is zy, where z is the number of students.

2. **Excluding the highest and lowest scores:**
- We need to find the total score of the class excluding the highest and lowest scores. The total score of the class is zy, and the sum of the highest and lowest scores is 2x. Therefore, the total score excluding the highest and lowest scores is zy - 2x.

3. **Calculating the average excluding the highest and lowest scores:**
- After excluding the highest and lowest scores, the number of students left is z - 2 (since we removed 2 students).
- The average score for these remaining students is the total score of these students divided by their number, which is (zy - 2x)/(z - 2).

Therefore, the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers is given by the expression (zy - 2x)/(z - 2).

The correct answer is {D}.
Final Answer: d

Question: Jerry purchased a 1-year $5,000 bond that paid an annual interest rate of 12% compounded every six months. How much interest had this bond accrued at maturity? # Answer option: ['A)$5102', 'B)$618', 'C)$216', 'D)$202', 'E)$200']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
To determine the interest accrued by the bond at maturity, we need to focus on the principal amount, the interest rate, and the compounding frequency. These elements are essential for calculating the total interest accrued over the bond's term.

### Key Facts:
$5,000 bond
annual interest rate of 12%
compounded every six months

### Reformatted Question:
Jerry purchased a 1-year $5,000 bond that paid an annual interest rate of 12% compounded every six months. How much interest had this bond accrued at maturity?
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
Jerry purchased a 1-year $5,000 bond that paid an annual interest rate of 12% compounded every six months. How much interest had this bond accrued at maturity?
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To determine how much interest the bond accrued at maturity, we need to calculate the compound interest for the bond.

Step 1: Identify the principal, rate, and compounding frequency.
- The principal amount is $5,000.
- The annual interest rate is 12%.
- The interest is compounded every six months.

Step 2: Determine the interest rate per compounding period.
Since the interest is compounded every six months, there are 2 compounding periods in a year. Therefore, the interest rate per period is:
12% annual rate / 2 = 6% per period.

Step 3: Calculate the compound interest using the formula:
\[ A = P \left(1 + \frac{r}{n}\right)^{nt} \]
Where:
- \( A \) is the amount of money accumulated after n years, including interest.
- \( P \) is the principal amount ($5,000).
- \( r \) is the annual interest rate (0.12).
- \( n \) is the number of times that interest is compounded per year (2).
- \( t \) is the time the money is invested for in years (1).

Plugging in the values:
\[ A = 5000 \left(1 + \frac{0.12}{2}\right)^{2 \times 1} \]
\[ A = 5000 \left(1 + 0.06\right)^2 \]
\[ A = 5000 \times 1.06^2 \]
\[ A = 5000 \times 1.1236 \]
\[ A = 5618 \]

Step 4: Calculate the interest accrued.
The interest accrued is the total amount minus the principal:
Interest = \( A - P = 5618 - 5000 = 618 \).

Therefore, the interest accrued at maturity is {B)$618}.
Final Answer: b)618
Ground Truth Answer: b

### Fact Extraction Reasoning:

### Reformatted Question:
64 boys and 40 girls form a group for social work. During their membership drive, the same number of boys and girls joined the group. How many members does the group have now, if the ratio of boys to girls is 4:3? # Answer option: ['A)277', 'B)288', 'C)200', 'D)277', 'E)168']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
64 boys and 40 girls form a group for social work. During their membership drive, the same number of boys and girls joined the group. How many members does the group have now, if the ratio of boys to girls is 4:3? # Answer option: ['A)277', 'B)288', 'C)200', 'D)277', 'E)168']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To solve this problem, we need to determine the number of new members that joined the group and then calculate the total number of members in the group.

1. **Initial Group Composition:**
- There are 64 boys and 40 girls in the group initially.

2. **Membership Drive:**
- During the membership drive, the same number of boys and girls joined the group. Let's denote the number of boys and girls who joined as \( x \).

3. **New Group Composition:**
- After the membership drive, the number of boys becomes \( 64 + x \) and the number of girls becomes \( 40 + x \).

4. **Ratio of Boys to Girls:**
- The problem states that the new ratio of boys to girls is 4:3. Therefore, we can set up the equation:
\[
\frac{64 + x}{40 + x} = \frac{4}{3}
\]

5. **Solving the Equation:**
- Cross-multiply to solve for \( x \):
\[
3(64 + x) = 4(40 + x)
\]
\[
192 + 3x = 160 + 4x
\]
\[
192 - 160 = 4x - 3x
\]
\[
32 = x
\]

6. **Total Number of Members:**
- Now that we know \( x = 32 \), we can calculate the total number of members in the group:
- Total boys = \( 64 + 32 = 96 \)
- Total girls = \( 40 + 32 = 72 \)
- Total members = \( 96 + 72 = 168 \)

Therefore, the total number of members in the group now is {168}.

Question: The events A and B are independent. The probability that event A occurs is 0.6, and the probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is 0.96. What is the probability that event B occurs? # Answer option: ['A)0.5', 'B)0.6', 'C)0.7', 'D)0.8', 'E)0.9']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
To determine the probability that event B occurs, we need to focus on the given probabilities and the relationship between events A and B. The key facts are the probability of event A occurring, the probability of at least one of the events A or B occurring, and the independence of events A and B. These facts are essential to calculate the probability of event B.

### Key Facts:
events A and B are independent
probability that event A occurs is 0.6
probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is 0.96

### Reformatted Question:
The events A and B are independent. The probability that event A occurs is 0.6, and the probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is 0.96. What is the probability that event B occurs? # Answer option: ['A)0.5', 'B)0.6', 'C)0.7', 'D)0.8', 'E)0.9']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
The events A and B are independent. The probability that event A occurs is 0.6, and the probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is 0.96. What is the probability that event B occurs? # Answer option: ['A)0.5', 'B)0.6', 'C)0.7', 'D)0.8', 'E)0.9']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To find the probability that event B occurs, we can use the formula for the probability of the union of two independent events, A and B. The formula is:

P(A ∪ B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A ∩ B)

Since the events A and B are independent, the probability of both events occurring, P(A ∩ B), is the product of their individual probabilities:

P(A ∩ B) = P(A) * P(B)

Given:
- The probability that event A occurs is 0.6, so P(A) = 0.6.
- The probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is 0.96, so P(A ∪ B) = 0.96.

Substituting these values into the formula:

0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - (0.6 * P(B))

Simplifying the equation:

0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - 0.6P(B)

0.96 = 0.6 + P(B)(1 - 0.6)

0.96 = 0.6 + 0.4P(B)

Subtract 0.6 from both sides:

0.36 = 0.4P(B)

Divide both sides by 0.4 to solve for P(B):

P(B) = 0.36 / 0.4

P(B) = 0.9

Therefore, the probability that event B occurs is 0.9. The correct answer is {E}.
Final Answer: e
Ground Truth Answer: e
Question: On a test the passing students had an average of 83, while the failing students had an average of 55. If the overall class average was 76, what percent of the class passed? # Answer option: ['A)44%', 'B)66%', 'C)68%', 'D)72%', 'E)75%']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
To determine the percentage of the class that passed, we need to focus on the average scores of the passing and failing students, as well as the overall class average. These figures are essential to calculate the proportion of students who passed.

### Key Facts:
passing students had an average of 83
failing students had an average of 55
overall class average was 76

### Reformatted Question:
On a test the passing students had an average of 83, while the failing students had an average of 55. If the overall class average was 76, what percent of the class passed? # Answer option: ['A)44%', 'B)66%', 'C)68%', 'D)72%', 'E)75%']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
On a test the passing students had an average of 83, while the failing students had an average of 55. If the overall class average was 76, what percent of the class passed? # Answer option: ['A)44%', 'B)66%', 'C)68%', 'D)72%', 'E)75%']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To solve this problem, we need to determine the percentage of students who passed the test based on the given averages.

Let's denote:
- \( p \) as the percentage of students who passed.
- \( f \) as the percentage of students who failed.

Since the total percentage must equal 100%, we have:
\[ p + f = 100 \]

We are given:
- The average score of passing students is 83.
- The average score of failing students is 55.
- The overall class average is 76.

The overall class average can be expressed as a weighted average of the passing and failing students' averages:
\[ 83p + 55f = 76 \times 100 \]

Substituting \( f = 100 - p \) into the equation:
\[ 83p + 55(100 - p) = 7600 \]

Expanding and simplifying:
\[ 83p + 5500 - 55p = 7600 \]
\[ 28p = 2100 \]
\[ p = \frac{2100}{28} \]
\[ p = 75 \]

Therefore, 75% of the class passed the test.

The correct answer is {E)75%}.
Final Answer: e)75%
Ground Truth Answer: e

Question: The cross-section of a canal is shaped like a trapezium. If the canal is 10 m wide at the top and 6 m wide at the bottom and the area of cross-section is 640 square meters, the depth of cannel is? # Answer option: ['A)26', 'B)28', 'C)21', 'D)80', 'E)23']
### Fact Extraction Reasoning:
To determine the depth of the canal, we need to focus on the dimensions of the trapezium that form the cross-section of the canal. The essential information includes the width at the top, the width at the bottom, and the area of the cross-section. These values are necessary to calculate the depth using the formula for the area of a trapezium.

### Key Facts:
10 m wide at the top
6 m wide at the bottom
area of cross-section is 640 square meters

### Reformatted Question:
The cross-section of a canal is shaped like a trapezium. If the canal is 10 m wide at the top and 6 m wide at the bottom and the area of cross-section is 640 square meters, the depth of cannel is? # Answer option: ['A)26', 'B)28', 'C)21', 'D)80', 'E)23']
--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
The cross-section of a canal is shaped like a trapezium. If the canal is 10 m wide at the top and 6 m wide at the bottom and the area of cross-section is 640 square meters, the depth of cannel is? # Answer option: ['A)26', 'B)28', 'C)21', 'D)80', 'E)23']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To find the depth of the canal, we need to use the formula for the area of a trapezium, which is given by:

\[ \text{Area} = \frac{1}{2} \times (\text{Base}_1 + \text{Base}_2) \times \text{Height} \]

In this problem, the bases are the widths at the top and bottom of the canal, and the height is the depth of the canal.

Given:
- The top width (Base 1) is 10 m.
- The bottom width (Base 2) is 6 m.
- The area of the cross-section is 640 square meters.

We can substitute these values into the formula:

\[ 640 = \frac{1}{2} \times (10 + 6) \times \text{Depth} \]

Simplifying the equation:

\[ 640 = \frac{1}{2} \times 16 \times \text{Depth} \]

\[ 640 = 8 \times \text{Depth} \]

To find the depth, divide both sides by 8:

\[ \text{Depth} = \frac{640}{8} \]

\[ \text{Depth} = 80 \]

Therefore, the depth of the canal is 80 meters.

The correct answer is {D}.
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d

The second condition involves Sajal giving $10 to Arjun, resulting in Arjun having three times the amount left with Sajal. These conditions are essential to set up the equations needed to find the solution.

### Key Facts:
If Arun gives $30 to Sajal, the Sajal will have twice the money left with Arjun
if Sajal gives $10 to Arjun, Arjun will have thrice as much as is left with Sajal

--------------- End of Conversation ---------------
Arjun and Sajal are friends, each has some money. If Arun gives $30 to Sajal, the Sajal will have twice the money left with Arjun. But, if Sajal gives $10 to Arjun, Arjun will have thrice as much as is left with Sajal. How much money does each have? # Answer option: ['A)62, 35', 'B)62, 34', 'C)34, 62', 'D)42, 62', 'E)62, 42']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To solve this problem, we need to set up equations based on the given facts.

Let's denote the amount of money Arjun has as \( A \) and the amount Sajal has as \( S \).

1. From , if Arjun gives $30 to Sajal, then Sajal will have twice the money left with Arjun. This can be expressed as:
\[
S + 30 = 2(A - 30)
\]
Simplifying this equation:
\[
S + 30 = 2A - 60
\]
\[
S = 2A - 90
\]

2. From , if Sajal gives $10 to Arjun, then Arjun will have thrice as much as is left with Sajal. This can be expressed as:
\[
A + 10 = 3(S - 10)
\]
Simplifying this equation:
\[
A + 10 = 3S - 30
\]
\[
A = 3S - 40
\]

Now, we have two equations:
1. \( S = 2A - 90 \)
2. \( A = 3S - 40 \)

Substitute the expression for \( S \) from the first equation into the second equation:
\[
A = 3(2A - 90) - 40
\]
\[
A = 6A - 270 - 40
\]
\[
A = 6A - 310
\]
\[
310 = 6A - A
\]
\[
310 = 5A
\]
\[
A = 62
\]

Now, substitute \( A = 62 \) back into the equation for \( S \):
\[
S = 2(62) - 90
\]
\[
S = 124 - 90
\]
\[
S = 34
\]

Therefore, Arjun has $62 and Sajal has $34. The correct answer is {B)62, 34}.
Final Answer: b)62 34

2. Each song was selected 5 times.

- Each student selects 2 songs, which means each student contributes 2 selections to the total count.

### Fact Extraction Reasoning:

### Key Facts:

### Reformatted Question:
A flagstaff 17.5 metre high casts a shadow of length 40.25 metre. The height of building, which casts a shadow of length 28.75 metre under similar conditions will be: # Answer option: ['A)12 metre', 'B)12.5 metre', 'C)13.5 metre', 'D)14 metre', 'E)15 metre']

A flagstaff 17.5 metre high casts a shadow of length 40.25 metre. The height of building, which casts a shadow of length 28.75 metre under similar conditions will be: # Answer option: ['A)12 metre', 'B)12.5 metre', 'C)13.5 metre', 'D)14 metre', 'E)15 metre']
--------------- Extracted Question ---------------

To solve this problem, we need to use the concept of similar triangles, as the conditions under which the shadows are cast are similar.

1. We know that a flagstaff 17.5 metre high casts a shadow of length 40.25 metre. This gives us the ratio of height to shadow length for the flagstaff:
\[
\text{Ratio for flagstaff} = \frac{17.5}{40.25}
\]

2. We need to find the height of a building that casts a shadow of length 28.75 metre under similar conditions. Let the height of the building be \( h \).

3. Since the conditions are similar, the ratio of the height of the building to its shadow length should be the same as that of the flagstaff:
\[
\frac{h}{28.75} = \frac{17.5}{40.25}
\]

4. Solving for \( h \), we cross-multiply:
\[
h = \frac{17.5 \times 28.75}{40.25}
\]

5. Calculating the above expression:
\[
h = \frac{17.5 \times 28.75}{40.25} = \frac{503.125}{40.25} \approx 12.5
\]

Thus, the height of the building is approximately 12.5 metres. Therefore, the correct answer is {B}.
